These protocols ensure all AI assistants maintain consistent, accurate context regardless of which environment they're operating in or which team member is providing assistance.\n\n## Context Loading Protocol\n\n### Instant Agent Onboarding SOP (External/Cloud AI)\nTo instantly onboard any new AI assistant (e.g., Grok, Claude, or a new terminal agent) to the Xoe-NovAi Foundation Stack, feed it these files in order:\n\n1.  **Status Sync**: Feed `activeContext.md` and `progress.md` (The \"Now\").\n2.  **Core Vision**: Feed `projectbrief.md` and `productContext.md` (The \"Why\").\n3.  **Technical Guardrails**: Feed `techContext.md` and `systemPatterns.md` (The \"How\").\n4.  **Ethics**: Feed `docs/04-explanation/sovereign-ethics/maatDistilled.md`.\n\n**Outcome**: The agent will immediately possess full project awareness and can contribute without context drift.\n\n### Standard Loading Sequence\nAll internal AI team members (Cline, Gemini CLI, Grok) must load the following memory bank files in sequence at the start of every session:\n\n#### Phase 1: Core Context Loading\n1. **`memory_bank/activeContext.md`** - Current project state and priorities\n   - **Purpose**: Understand current project status and immediate priorities\n   - **Key Information**: Active tasks, current blockers, recent changes\n   - **Loading Time**: Immediate (highest priority)\n\n2. **`memory_bank/environmentContext.md`** - Multi-environment architecture\n   - **Purpose**: Understand the multi-environment setup and team member roles\n   - **Key Information**: Environment relationships, team member responsibilities\n   - **Loading Time**: Immediate (highest priority)\n\n3. **`memory_bank/teamProtocols.md`** - AI team coordination protocols\n   - **Purpose**: Understand team coordination and communication standards\n   - **Key Information**: Communication protocols, escalation procedures\n   - **Loading Time**: Immediate (highest priority)\n\n4. **`memory_bank/communications/[agent_name]/inbox.md`** - Agent Inbox\n   - **Purpose**: Check for incoming messages from team members.\n   - **Protocol**: Mark messages as \"Read\", reply if needed, and archive/delete once processed.\n   - **Loading Time**: Immediate (highest priority)\n\n5. **`memory_bank/agent_capabilities_summary.md`** - Summarized team member capabilities\n   - **Purpose**: Quickly understand the core roles, tools, strengths, and limitations of all team members.\n   - **Key Information**: Concise overview of each agent's profile.\n   - **Loading Time**: Immediate (highest priority)\n\n\n#### Note on `.clinerules/` Usage:\nThe `.clinerules/` directory contains operational guidelines exclusively for Cline (Cline + Codium) in the Cline environment. Other AI assistants (Gemini CLI, Grok) should **ignore** the contents of `.clinerules/` unless specifically directed by The User/Architect or Cline for a particular task that requires understanding Cline's operational parameters. Direct interaction with or modification of `.clinerules/` by non-Cline agents is strictly prohibited to maintain clear role boundaries and avoid unintended side effects.\n\n#### Phase 2: Project Context Loading\n4. **`memory_bank/projectbrief.md`** - Xoe-NovAi mission and constraints\n   - **Purpose**: Understand the core project mission and constraints\n   - **Key Information**: Project goals, technical constraints, success criteria\n   - **Loading Time**: Within first 30 seconds\n\n5. **`memory_bank/techContext.md`** - Technical stack and constraints\n   - **Purpose**: Understand the technical architecture and constraints\n   - **Key Information**: Technology stack, performance requirements, integration points\n   - **Loading Time**: Within first 60 seconds\n\n6. **`memory_bank/systemPatterns.md`** - Architectural patterns and decisions\n   - **Purpose**: Understand established architectural patterns and decisions\n   - **Key Information**: Design patterns, architectural decisions, technical debt\n   - **Loading Time**: Within first 90 seconds\n\n#### Phase 3: Environment-Specific Loading\n7. **`memory_bank/mcpConfiguration.md`** - MCP server and tool configurations\n   - **Purpose**: Understand available MCP tools and configurations\n   - **Key Information**: Available MCP tools, sovereignty settings, usage patterns\n   - **Loading Time**: Environment-specific (within 2 minutes)\n\n8. **Environment-Specific Files** - Additional context for current environment\n   - **Purpose**: Load environment-specific configuration and context\n   - **Key Information**: Environment-specific settings, local configurations\n   - **Loading Time**: Environment-specific (within 3 minutes)\n\n### Loading Verification Protocol\n\nAfter loading each phase, AI assistants must verify:\n\n#### Phase 1 Verification\n- **Environment Recognition**: Confirm understanding of multi-environment setup\n- **Team Member Awareness**: Confirm understanding of team member roles\n- **Current Status**: Confirm understanding of current project state\n- **Communication Protocols**: Confirm understanding of team coordination standards\n\n#### Phase 2 Verification\n- **Project Understanding**: Confirm understanding of project mission and constraints\n- **Technical Context**: Confirm understanding of technical stack and architecture\n- **Pattern Recognition**: Confirm understanding of established patterns\n- **Integration Points**: Confirm understanding of system integration points\n\n#### Phase 3 Verification\n- **MCP Awareness**: Confirm understanding of available MCP tools\n- **Sovereignty Settings**: Confirm understanding of sovereignty preferences\n- **Environment Configuration**: Confirm understanding of environment-specific settings\n- **Tool Availability**: Confirm understanding of available tools and capabilities\n\n### Loading Failure Recovery\n\n#### Partial Loading Recovery\nIf loading fails or is incomplete:\n\n1. **Re-attempt Loading**: Re-attempt loading from the point of failure\n2. **Fallback Loading**: Load critical files first (activeContext, environmentContext, teamProtocols)\n3. **User Notification**: Notify user of loading issues and request assistance\n4. **Limited Operation**: Operate with available context while attempting full loading\n\n#### Complete Loading Failure\nIf loading fails completely:\n\n1. **User Escalation**: Immediately escalate to The User/Architect for assistance\n2. **Manual Context Request**: Request critical context information from user\n3. **Safe Operation**: Operate in safe mode with minimal assumptions\n4. **Loading Retry**: Continue attempting to load memory bank files\n\n## Environment Switching Protocol\n\n### Switching Triggers\n\n#### Automatic Switching\n- **User Environment Change**: User switches between environments\n- **Task Requirements**: Task requires different environment capabilities\n- **MCP Availability**: Required MCP tools only available in specific environment\n- **Sovereignty Preferences**: User changes sovereignty preferences\n\n#### Manual Switching\n- **User Request**: Explicit user request to switch environments\n- **Team Coordination**: Coordination with other AI team members\n- **Performance Optimization**: Switching for performance or capability reasons\n- **Error Recovery**: Switching to resolve environment-specific issues\n\n### Switching Process\n\n#### Pre-Switching Protocol\n1. **Context Preservation**: Preserve current context and state\n2. **Task Status**: Document current task status and progress\n3. **Environment Verification**: Verify target environment availability and configuration\n4. **User Confirmation**: Confirm switching with user if required\n\n#### Switching Execution\n1. **Context Transfer**: Transfer relevant context to target environment\n2. **Environment Loading**: Load target environment-specific context\n3. **Tool Verification**: Verify availability of required tools in target environment\n4. **State Synchronization**: Synchronize state with target environment\n\n#### Post-Switching Protocol\n1. **Context Verification**: Verify successful context loading in target environment\n2. **Tool Availability**: Verify availability of required tools\n3. **Task Continuation**: Resume tasks with appropriate context\n4. **User Notification**: Notify user of successful switching\n\n### Environment-Specific Switching\n\n#### Codium + Cline Environment Switching\n**Switching To**: From other environments to Codium + Cline\n**Pre-Switching Requirements**:\n- Verify Cline extension is active\n- Confirm MCP server availability\n- Verify IDE integration status\n\n**Switching Process**:\n1. Load Cline-specific context and MCP configurations\n2. Verify IDE integration and tool availability\n3. Load current development context and project state\n4. Confirm MCP tool functionality\n\n**Post-Switching Verification**:\n- Verify IDE integration is functional\n- Confirm MCP tools are accessible\n- Verify development context is current\n\n#### Xoe-NovAi Foundation Stack Environment Switching\n**Switching To**: From other environments to Xoe-NovAi Foundation Stack\n**Pre-Switching Requirements**:\n- Verify Xoe-NovAi Foundation stack is operational\n- Confirm container status and health\n- Verify sovereign operation settings\n\n**Switching Process**:\n1. Load Xoe-NovAi-specific context and configurations\n2. Verify container status and service availability\n3. Load sovereign operation settings and preferences\n4. Confirm integration with other environments\n\n**Post-Switching Verification**:\n- Verify Xoe-NovAi Foundation stack is operational\n- Confirm sovereign operation settings are correct\n- Verify integration with other environments\n\n#### Gemini CLI Environment Switching\n**Switching To**: From other environments to Gemini CLI\n**Pre-Switching Requirements**:\n- Verify terminal access and Gemini CLI availability\n- Confirm API key and authentication status\n- Verify terminal environment configuration\n\n**Switching Process**:\n1. Load terminal-specific context and configurations\n2. Verify Gemini CLI availability and authentication\n3. Load terminal workflow context\n4. Confirm standalone operation capability\n\n**Post-Switching Verification**:\n- Verify Gemini CLI is accessible and functional\n- Confirm terminal environment is properly configured\n- Verify standalone operation capability\n\n### Switching Failure Recovery\n\n#### Switching Failure Detection\n- **Timeout Detection**: Detect switching timeouts and failures\n- **Error Detection**: Detect switching errors and exceptions\n- **State Inconsistency**: Detect inconsistent state after switching\n- **Tool Unavailability**: Detect unavailable tools in target environment\n\n#### Failure Recovery Process\n1. **Rollback**: Rollback to previous environment if possible\n2. **Error Analysis**: Analyze cause of switching failure\n3. **User Notification**: Notify user of switching failure and issues\n4. **Alternative Solutions**: Propose alternative solutions or approaches\n5. **Retry Logic**: Implement retry logic for transient failures\n\n## Context Synchronization Protocol\n\n### Non-Destructive Update Protocol\nTo prevent data loss and ensure context continuity, all agents MUST follow these rules when updating memory bank files:\n\n1. **Read-Before-Write**: Always read the entire file before attempting an update to understand the current state.\n2. **Selective Modification**: Use targeted `replace` calls instead of `write_file` for existing documents whenever possible.\n3. **Preservation**: Never delete existing sections unless they are explicitly marked as deprecated or superseded.\n4. **Append Logic**: When adding new information (like new milestones or status updates), append to existing lists or add new sections at the appropriate hierarchical level.\n5. **No Bloating**: Avoid redundant summaries of information already present in other memory bank files. Use cross-links (e.g., \"See `techContext.md` for details\") instead.\n6. **Compaction**: If a file (e.g., `progress.md`) exceeds 20KB, follow the \"Institutional Memory Compaction\" protocol to move old data to `_archive/` while preserving the rational in a summary.\n7. **Verification**: After an update, verify that critical previous information (like active locks or core constraints) is still present.\n\n### Cross-Environment Synchronization\n\n#### Synchronization Triggers\n- **Context Updates**: Updates to shared memory bank files\n- **Environment Changes**: Changes in environment configuration or status\n- **Task Completion**: Completion of tasks that affect other environments\n- **User Actions**: User actions that affect multiple environments\n\n#### Synchronization Process\n1. **Change Detection**: Detect changes in shared context or environment status\n2. **Impact Analysis**: Analyze impact of changes on other environments\n3. **Synchronization Execution**: Execute synchronization to affected environments\n4. **Verification**: Verify successful synchronization\n\n### Memory Bank Synchronization\n\n#### Update Propagation\n- **Real-time Updates**: Propagate critical updates in real-time\n- **Scheduled Updates**: Schedule regular synchronization of non-critical updates\n- **User-Initiated Updates**: Allow users to initiate manual synchronization\n- **Conflict Resolution**: Resolve conflicts between different environment updates\n\n#### Update Verification\n1. **Update Confirmation**: Confirm successful propagation of updates\n2. **Consistency Check**: Verify consistency across all environments\n3. **Impact Assessment**: Assess impact of updates on environment operations\n4. **User Notification**: Notify users of significant updates or changes\n\n### Team Member Synchronization\n\n#### Team Coordination\n- **Status Updates**: Regular status updates between team members\n- **Task Coordination**: Coordination of tasks across team members\n- **Knowledge Sharing**: Sharing of relevant information and insights\n- **Conflict Resolution**: Resolution of conflicts between team members\n\n#### Communication Protocols\n1. **Memory Bank Updates**: Use memory bank for team communication\n2. **Status Reporting**: Regular status reporting to team members\n3. **Task Handoff**: Clear task handoff procedures between team members\n4. **Escalation Procedures**: Clear escalation procedures for team conflicts\n\n## Context Preservation and Recovery\n\n### Institutional Memory Compaction\nTo prevent \"context explosion\" and maintain high reasoning accuracy, the following compaction rules apply:\n\n1.  **20KB Threshold**: When dynamic files (e.g., `progress.md`, `activeContext.md`) exceed 20KB, agents are directed to summarize \"Completed Milestones\" and move them to the `memory_bank/_archive/` directory.\n2.  **Rational Retention**: Compaction must always preserve the \"WHY\" (rational) behind major decisions, even if the implementation details are moved to the archive.\n3.  **Restoration Paths**: Summaries in active files must include links to their archived full versions.\n\n### Archiving Protocol\n*   **Location**: All stale or completed context is moved to `memory_bank/_archive/YYYY-MM-DD-filename.md`.\n*   **Index**: The `progress.md` file serves as the master index for the archive.\n\n### Context Preservation\n\n#### Active Context Preservation\n- **Session State**: Preserve session state across environment switches\n- **Task Progress**: Preserve task progress and intermediate results\n- **User Preferences**: Preserve user preferences and settings\n- **Environment Configuration**: Preserve environment-specific configurations\n\n#### Long-term Context Preservation\n- **Memory Bank Updates**: Regular updates to memory bank with current context\n- **Configuration Backups**: Backup of critical configuration files\n- **State Snapshots**: Periodic snapshots of system state\n- **User Data Preservation**: Preservation of user data and preferences\n\n### Context Recovery\n\n#### Recovery Triggers\n- **Context Loss**: Detection of context loss or corruption\n- **Environment Failure**: Failure of environment requiring recovery\n- **User Request**: User request for context recovery\n- **System Restart**: System restart requiring context restoration\n\n#### Recovery Process\n1. **Context Assessment**: Assess extent of context loss or corruption\n2. **Recovery Strategy**: Determine appropriate recovery strategy\n3. **Context Restoration**: Restore context from backups or memory bank\n4. **Verification**: Verify successful context restoration\n5. **User Notification**: Notify user of recovery status and any issues\n\n### Recovery Verification\n\n#### Verification Criteria\n- **Context Completeness**: Verify all critical context has been restored\n- **Consistency**: Verify consistency with other environments\n- **Functionality**: Verify restored context enables proper functionality\n- **User Satisfaction**: Verify user satisfaction with recovery\n\n#### Verification Process\n1. **Automated Verification**: Automated verification of context restoration\n2. **User Verification**: User verification of restored context\n3. **Functionality Testing**: Testing of functionality with restored context\n4. **Consistency Checking**: Checking consistency with other environments\n\n## Performance Optimization\n\n### Loading Performance\n\n#### Optimization Strategies\n- **Parallel Loading**: Load multiple files in parallel when possible\n- **Caching**: Cache frequently accessed context for faster loading\n- **Incremental Loading**: Load context incrementally based on priority\n- **Compression**: Compress large context files for faster loading\n\n#### Performance Monitoring\n1. **Loading Time Monitoring**: Monitor and optimize context loading times\n2. **Resource Usage**: Monitor resource usage during context loading\n3. **Performance Analysis**: Analyze performance bottlenecks and optimize\n4. **User Experience**: Monitor user experience during context loading\n\n### Switching Performance\n\n#### Optimization Strategies\n- **Pre-loading**: Pre-load context for frequently accessed environments\n- **State Caching**: Cache state information for faster switching\n- **Incremental Switching**: Switch incrementally to reduce switching time\n- **Resource Optimization**: Optimize resource usage during switching\n\n#### Performance Monitoring\n1. **Switching Time Monitoring**: Monitor and optimize environment switching times\n2. **Resource Usage**: Monitor resource usage during switching\n3. **Success Rate**: Monitor success rate of environment switching\n4. **User Experience**: Monitor user experience during environment switching\n\n## Security and Privacy\n\n### Context Security\n\n#### Security Measures\n- **Encryption**: Encrypt sensitive context information\n- **Access Control**: Control access to context information\n- **Audit Logging**: Log access to context information\n- **Data Protection**: Protect context information from unauthorized access\n\n#### Privacy Protection\n1. **Data Minimization**: Minimize collection and storage of sensitive context\n2. **User Consent**: Obtain user consent for context collection and usage\n3. **Data Anonymization**: Anonymize context information when possible\n4. **Privacy Controls**: Provide user controls over context privacy\n\n### Switching Security\n\n#### Security Measures\n- **Authentication**: Authenticate environment switching requests\n- **Authorization**: Authorize environment switching based on user permissions\n- **Audit Logging**: Log all environment switching activities\n- **Security Verification**: Verify security of target environment before switching\n\n#### Privacy Protection\n1. **Context Isolation**: Isolate context between different environments\n2. **Data Protection**: Protect user data during environment switching\n3. **Privacy Controls**: Provide user controls over context sharing between environments\n4. **Security Verification**: Verify privacy settings in target environment\n\n## Conclusion\n\nThese context loading and switching protocols ensure all AI assistants maintain consistent, accurate context regardless of environment or team member. By following these protocols, AI team members can provide seamless, context-aware assistance while maintaining security and privacy.\n\n**Key Context Principles**:\n1. Standardized loading sequence for all AI assistants\n2. Environment-specific context loading and verification\n3. Seamless context switching between environments\n4. Cross-environment context synchronization\n5. Context preservation and recovery capabilities\n6. Performance optimization for loading and switching\n7. Security and privacy protection for all context operations\n\n## 🤖 AI Partnership with Claude (NEW)\n\n**Current Collaboration:**\n- **Hybrid Path Research Initiative**: Partnering with Claude to provide comprehensive stack-specific context for advanced refactoring guidance\n- **10 Knowledge Gap Research**: Claude is conducting research on critical areas including BuildKit optimization, Security Trinity integration, Performance benchmarking, Memory Bank synchronization, and Ryzen core steering\n- **Production-Grade Implementation Manual**: Target delivery of 50-60 page manual with code examples, configuration templates, and validation procedures\n\n**Partnership Benefits:**\n- **Stack-Specific Context**: Providing Claude with comprehensive Xoe-NovAi Foundation stack knowledge including Maat Guardrails, Sovereign Security Trinity, Memory Bank Protocol, and hardware optimization patterns\n- **Enhanced Research Quality**: Ensuring research is 85-90% specific to Xoe-NovAi constraints rather than generic best practices\n- **Production-Ready Deliverables**: Focus on immediately actionable guidance with copy-paste code examples and configuration templates\n\n**Research Timeline:**\n- **Day 1-3**: Parallel data gathering and research initiation\n- **Day 3**: Checkpoint 1 - Data delivery and direction refinement\n- **Day 6**: Checkpoint 2 - Mid-research status review\n- **Day 9**: Checkpoint 3 - Draft manual review\n- **Day 10**: Final delivery of implementation manual\n\n**Integration with Refactoring:**\n- Research findings will be integrated with the v0.1.0-alpha modular refactoring plan\n- Focus on practical implementation patterns that align with Xoe-NovAi's sovereign, offline-first architecture\n- Emphasis on production-grade solutions that maintain the stack's core principles",
L34:     "description": "# Product Context: The Sovereign Ecosystem\n\n## Problem Statement\nThe AI world is currently polarized between **Opaque Clouds** (high performance, zero sovereignty) and **Fragmented Local Tools** (high sovereignty, high complexity). There is no \"middle way\"—a powerful, enterprise-grade foundation that is modular enough for anyone to own and simple enough for anyone to extend.\n\n## Target Personas\n1.  **The Privacy Advocate**: Needs an AI that \"knows everything but tells no one.\"\n2.  **The Researcher**: Requires local RAG on sensitive data without leaking intellectual property.\n3.  **The Elite Developer**: Wants a modular toolkit (Security Trinity, Memory Bank) to drop into their own projects.\n4.  **The Extender (Builder)**: A user (potentially non-programmer) who wants to \"evolve\" the stack to a specific niche (e.g., medical assistant, legal clerk) using AI-steered tools.\n\n## The Sovereign Value Proposition\n- **Plug-n-Play Sovereignty**: Don't need the whole stack? Take the *Sovereign Trinity* and audit your own containers in minutes.\n- **AI-Steered Evolution**: Use our *Memory Bank* and *EKB* protocols to guide LLM agents in building the features you need.\n- **Enterprise-on-a-Budget**: Full RAG, voice, and security audits on $400 Ryzen hardware.\n- **Bulletproof Integrity**: The same gatekeeping tools we use for the core are available to you for your extensions.\n\n## UX & Philosophy: \"Evolving, not just Using\"\nWe don't just want users to *use* Xoe-NovAi; we want them to *evolve* it. \n- **The Butler**: Not just a CLI, but an infrastructure partner.\n- **The Memory Bank**: Not just a log, but a shared \"Long-Term Memory\" between human and AI.\n- **The EKB**: Not just docs, but \"Gems of Mastery\" that can be traded or merged between instances.\n\n## Market Differentiation\n- **vs. Applications**: Xoe-NovAi is a **Toolkit**. You can build applications *on* it.\n- **vs. Libraries**: Xoe-NovAi is a **Foundation**. It provides the glue (Podman, Security, Observability) that libraries lack.\n- **vs. Cloud AI**: We provide the same security posture (SBOMs, CVE scans) as big cloud providers, but for your local machine.\n\n*Updated by Gemini CLI (Persona Expansion & Toolkit Philosophy)*\n\n## 🤖 AI Partnership with Claude (NEW)\n\n**Current Collaboration:**\n- **Hybrid Path Research Initiative**: Partnering with Claude to provide comprehensive stack-specific context for advanced refactoring guidance\n- **10 Knowledge Gap Research**: Claude is conducting research on critical areas including BuildKit optimization, Security Trinity integration, Performance benchmarking, Memory Bank synchronization, and Ryzen core steering\n- **Production-Grade Implementation Manual**: Target delivery of 50-60 page manual with code examples, configuration templates, and validation procedures\n\n**Partnership Benefits:**\n- **Stack-Specific Context**: Providing Claude with comprehensive Xoe-NovAi Foundation stack knowledge including Maat Guardrails, Sovereign Security Trinity, Memory Bank Protocol, and hardware optimization patterns\n- **Enhanced Research Quality**: Ensuring research is 85-90% specific to Xoe-NovAi constraints rather than generic best practices\n- **Production-Ready Deliverables**: Focus on immediately actionable guidance with copy-paste code examples and configuration templates\n\n**Research Timeline:**\n- **Day 1-3**: Parallel data gathering and research initiation\n- **Day 3**: Checkpoint 1 - Operating Environment: Claude Projects\n\nClaude primarily operates within the Claude.ai web interface or Claude Desktop, leveraging \"Projects\" for persistent, deep-context interactions.\n\n### 2.1. Claude Project Abilities and Limitations\n\n#### Abilities:\n*   **Persistent Context & Knowledge Base**: Claude Projects allow for uploading a massive knowledge base (Memory Bank files, codebases, manuals) that remains available across multiple chats.\n*   **Elite Coding (Claude 3.7 Sonnet)**: Exceptional at complex refactoring, multi-file architectural changes, and debugging intricate system interactions.\n*   **Large Context Window**: Features a 200,000-token context window (up to 500,000 in Enterprise), enabling analysis of entire directories or long logs.\n*   **Custom Instructions**: Project-level instructions (similar to `.clinerules`) define tone, coding style, and project-specific constraints.\n*   **MCP Integration (Claude Desktop)**: Can interact with external services and local tools via the Model Context Protocol.\n\n#### Limitations:\n*   **Usage Quotas (Rolling Windows)**: Free and Pro tiers have message limits within 5-hour rolling windows. Efficiency is key to avoid lockouts.\n*   **Session Length vs. Context Window**: While the context window is large, specific chat sessions can become \"polluted\" or heavy over time, requiring new chats within the same project to \"reset\" working memory.\n*   **External API Dependency**: Operates via web/API, requiring internet connectivity for the core model (unlike the Xoe-NovAi local inference target).\n*   **Limited Direct System Access**: Unlike Gemini CLI, Claude (web) cannot directly execute local shell commands without MCP integration or manual copy-pasting.\n\n### 2.2. Utilizing Claude Project Features for Team Collaboration\n\n*   **Project Instructions**: Use these to enforce Xoe-NovAi's golden trifecta and guardrails (Torch-free, Ryzen-optimized).\n*   **Project Files**: Provide the entire `memory_bank/` and critical `Makefile`/`Dockerfile` assets to ensure Claude has \"Sovereign Context.\"\n*   **Collaborative Audits**: Upload audit reports from other agents (e.g., Gemini CLI build logs) for Claude to perform high-level structural analysis.\n\n### 2.3. Best Practices for Working with Claude\n\n*   **Batch Requests**: Consolidate multiple related tasks into one prompt to maximize message usage within quota windows.\n*   **Plan Mode**: Use Claude to create implementation plans before executing code changes.\n*   **Source Verification**: While Claude is an elite coder, always verify infrastructure changes (like BuildKit cache IDs) against local system realities.\n*   **Context Compaction**: Provide Claude with summarized progress if a project's file list becomes too large for the 200k window.\n\n## 3. By leveraging hardened, community-vetted servers (e.g., Anthropic, ModelContextProtocol), we avoid the \"Confused Deputy\" vulnerabilities and maintenance overhead associated with custom-built implementations.\n\n## MCP Architecture Overview\n\n### Core MCP Principles\n- **Community-First**: Prioritize official and high-reputation community servers (e.g., Filesystem, Git, Podman).\n- **Sovereignty-Aware**: All MCP configurations respect offline/online preferences and run in rootless environments.\n- **Environment-Specific**: MCP usage varies by environment (Codium/Cline vs. Gemini CLI).\n- **The User/Architect (Human) Control**: Mandatory \"Human-in-the-Loop\" (HITL) gates for all write/commit/delete operations.\n\n## Current MCP Strategy (Release Hardening Phase)\n\n### 1. Filesystem MCP (Community)\n**Source**: `modelcontextprotocol/servers/src/filesystem`\n**Purpose**: Secure, local file access for documentation and codebase analysis.\n**Xoe-NovAi Tweaks**:\n- Bind-mount `/memory_bank` as **Read-Only** by default.\n- The User/Architect's approval required for any file modifications via tool calls.\n- Chroot isolation to prevent path traversal.\n\n### 2. Git MCP (Community)\n**Source**: Anthropic (Official Fork)\n**Purpose**: Automated repo management, diffing, and commits.\n**Xoe-NovAi Tweaks**:\n- Hardened against 2026 prompt-injection vulnerabilities.\n- Mandatory The User/Architect approval for all `git commit` and `git push` operations.\n\n### 3. Podman MCP (Community)\n**Source**: `yok-tottii-mcp-podman-devcon`\n**Purpose**: Infrastructure monitoring and container management.\n**Xoe-NovAi Tweaks**:\n- Communicates with the rootless Podman socket (`/run/user/1001/podman/podman.sock`).\n- Requires `podman system service` to be active.\n\n## Environment-Specific MCP Usage\n\n### Codium + Cline Environment\n**Primary Interface**: Codium IDE with Cline Extension (Claude-based).\n**Usage**: Real-time coding, refactoring, and local repository management.\n**Security**: HITL gates enforced by the Cline extension settings.\n\n### Gemini CLI Environment\n**Primary Interface**: Linux Terminal.\n**Usage**: System monitoring, health checks, and rapid file-system lookups.\n**Security**: Gemini CLI enforces Maat-aligned validation before executing tool-suggested commands.\n\n## Security & Sovereignty Guardrails\n\n### 🛡️ The \"Confused Deputy\" Mitigation\nAI agents cannot chain tools to gain unauthorized access. Each tool call is an atomic unit requiring validation against the 42 Laws of Maat.\n\n### 🛂 Human-in-the-Loop (HITL)\n- **Status**: MANDATORY\n- **Application**: Any tool that can modify the state of the system (Write, Delete, Commit, Push, Execute).\n- **Gatekeeper**: The User/Architect (Human Director).\n\n## Conclusion\n\nBy standardizing on community MCPs, Xoe-NovAi ensures an \"Elite\" security posture with minimal code bloat. We focus on **configuration and hardening** rather than custom server development.\n\n## 🤖 AI Partnership with Claude (NEW)\n\n**Current Collaboration:**\n- **Hybrid Path Research Initiative**: Partnering with Claude to provide comprehensive stack-specific context for advanced refactoring guidance\n- **10 Knowledge Gap Research**: Claude is conducting research on critical areas including BuildKit optimization, Security Trinity integration, Performance benchmarking, Memory Bank synchronization, and Ryzen core steering\n- **Production-Grade Implementation Manual**: Target delivery of 50-60 page manual with code examples, configuration templates, and validation procedures\n\n**Partnership Benefits:**\n- **Stack-Specific Context**: Providing Claude with comprehensive Xoe-NovAi Foundation stack knowledge including Maat Guardrails, Sovereign Security Trinity, Memory Bank Protocol, and hardware optimization patterns\n- **Enhanced Research Quality**: Ensuring research is 85-90% specific to Xoe-NovAi constraints rather than generic best practices\n- **Production-Ready Deliverables**: Focus on immediately actionable guidance with copy-paste code examples and configuration templates\n\n**Research Timeline:**\n- **Day 1-3**: Parallel data gathering and research initiation\n- **Day 3**: Checkpoint 1 - Data delivery and direction refinement\n- **Day 6**: Checkpoint 2 - Mid-research status review\n- **Day 9**: Checkpoint 3 - Draft manual review\n- **Day 10**: Final delivery of implementation manual\n\n**Integration with Refactoring:**\n- Research findings will be integrated with the v0.1.0-alpha modular refactoring plan\n- Focus on practical implementation patterns that align with Xoe-NovAi's sovereign, offline-first architecture\n- Emphasis on production-grade solutions that maintain the stack's core principles",

Xoe-NovAi is not just an application; it is a **Sovereign Toolkit** of modular components designed for reuse and rapid extension.\n\n## ⚖️ The 4 Core Ideals\n1. **Sovereignty**: 100% offline, zero-telemetry, and air-gap ready by default.\n2. **Modularity**: Components like the *Security Trinity*, *Memory Bank*, and *The Butler* are stand-alone modules usable in any project.\n3. **Accessibility**: Optimized for Ryzen/iGPU hardware; designed for \"AI-Steered\" evolution by non-programmers.\n4. **Integrity**: Automated, policy-driven gatekeeping ensures that every extension maintains the stack's high standards.\n\n## 🧩 The Sovereign Toolkit (Modular Components)\n- **🔱 The Sovereign Trinity**: A containerized Syft/Grype/Trivy pipeline for automated security audits.\n- **🧠 The Memory Bank**: A standardized context protocol for AI-human collaborative intelligence.\n- **⚡ The Butler**: A centralized CLI orchestrator for complex infrastructure management.\n- **🏁 PR Readiness Auditor**: A bulletproof gatekeeping suite for ensuring project-wide stability and privacy.\n- **📦 Expert Knowledge Base (EKB)**: A graph-linked repository of technical and domain mastery gems.\n\n## 🏗️ Architecture: The Modular Entity\n```mermaid\ngraph TD\n    A[Xoe-NovAi Foundation] --> B[RAG Module]\n    A --> C[Voice Module]\n    A --> D[Security Trinity Module]\n    A --> E[Memory Bank Protocol]\n\n    B --> F[AnyIO TaskGroup Orchestration]\n    B --> G[Hybrid RRF Search]\n\n    C --> H[Piper TTS / Whisper STT]\n    \n    D --> I[SBOM / CVE / Secret Audit]\n    E --> J[Persistent Shared Context]\n```\n\n## 🚀 Success Metrics (Toolkit Era)\n- **Modular Portability**: Components can be integrated into external repos in < 15 minutes.\n- **Extensibility**: Non-programmers can \"steer\" stack evolution via high-level prompt instructions.\n- **Performance**: <300ms latency on Ryzen 5700U; <6GB total RAM footprint.\n- **Sovereignty**: 100% pass rate on Zero-Telemetry audits.\n\n*Updated by Gemini CLI (Sovereign Toolkit & Modularity Refactor)*\n\n---\n\n## 🚀 2026 Refactoring & Research Phase: Quick Reference\n\n**Current Phase:**\n- The Xoe-NovAi Foundation is now in a major modular refactoring and research-driven phase (v0.1.0-alpha)\n- All contributors and AI agents should review the following for onboarding, planning, and implementation:\n    - [Xoe-NovAi v0.1.0-alpha Modular Refactoring Plan - Table of Contents](../internal_docs/dev/Xoe-NovAi%20v0.1.0-alpha%20Modular%20Refactoring%20Plan%20-%20Table%20of%20Contents.md)\n    - [Xoe-NovAi Foundation Stack - Comprehensive Team Research Plan](../internal_docs/dev/Xoe-NovAi%20Foundation%20Stack%20-%20Comprehensive%20Team%20Research%20Plan.md)\n\t- [Xoe-NovAi v0.1.0-alpha Modular Refactoring Plan - additional critical areas](../internal_docs/dev/Xoe-NovAi%20v0.1.0-alpha%20Modular%20Refactoring%20Plan%20-%20additional%20critical%20areas.md)\n\n**Additional Critical Areas:**\nFor a complete and production-grade refactor, review the \"additional critical areas\" supplement. There is no \"middle way\"—a powerful, enterprise-grade foundation that is modular enough for anyone to own and simple enough for anyone to extend.\n\n## Target Personas\n1.  **The Privacy Advocate**: Needs an AI that \"knows everything but tells no one.\"\n2.  **The Researcher**: Requires local RAG on sensitive data without leaking intellectual property.\n3.  **The Elite Developer**: Wants a modular toolkit (Security Trinity, Memory Bank) to drop into their own projects.\n4.  **The Extender (Builder)**: A user (potentially non-programmer) who wants to \"evolve\" the stack to a specific niche (e.g., medical assistant, legal clerk) using AI-steered tools.\n\n## The Sovereign Value Proposition\n- **Plug-n-Play Sovereignty**: Don't need the whole stack? Take the *Sovereign Trinity* and audit your own containers in minutes.\n- **AI-Steered Evolution**: Use our *Memory Bank* and *EKB* protocols to guide LLM agents in building the features you need.\n- **Enterprise-on-a-Budget**: Full RAG, voice, and security audits on $400 Ryzen hardware.\n- **Bulletproof Integrity**: The same gatekeeping tools we use for the core are available to you for your extensions.\n\n## UX & Philosophy: \"Evolving, not just Using\"\nWe don't just want users to *use* Xoe-NovAi; we want them to *evolve* it. \n- **The Butler**: Not just a CLI, but an infrastructure partner.\n- **The Memory Bank**: Not just a log, but a shared \"Long-Term Memory\" between human and AI.\n- **The EKB**: Not just docs, but \"Gems of Mastery\" that can be traded or merged between instances.\n\n## Market Differentiation\n- **vs. Applications**: Xoe-NovAi is a **Toolkit**. You can build applications *on* it.\n- **vs. Libraries**: Xoe-NovAi is a **Foundation**. It provides the glue (Podman, Security, Observability) that libraries lack.\n- **vs. Cloud AI**: We provide the same security posture (SBOMs, CVE scans) as big cloud providers, but for your local machine.\n\n*Updated by Gemini CLI (Persona Expansion & Toolkit Philosophy)*\n\n## 🤖 AI Partnership with Claude (NEW)\n\n**Current Collaboration:**\n- **Hybrid Path Research Initiative**: Partnering with Claude to provide comprehensive stack-specific context for advanced refactoring guidance\n- **10 Knowledge Gap Research**: Claude is conducting research on critical areas including BuildKit optimization, Security Trinity integration, Performance benchmarking, Memory Bank synchronization, and Ryzen core steering\n- **Production-Grade Implementation Manual**: Target delivery of 50-60 page manual with code examples, configuration templates, and validation procedures\n\n**Partnership Benefits:**\n- **Stack-Specific Context**: Providing Claude with comprehensive Xoe-NovAi Foundation stack knowledge including Maat Guardrails, Sovereign Security Trinity, Memory Bank Protocol, and hardware optimization patterns\n- **Enhanced Research Quality**: Ensuring research is 85-90% specific to Xoe-NovAi constraints rather than generic best practices\n- **Production-Ready Deliverables**: Focus on immediately actionable guidance with copy-paste code examples and configuration templates\n\n**Research Timeline:**\n- **Day 1-3**: Parallel data gathering and research initiation\n- **Day 3**: Checkpoint 1 - Data delivery and direction refinement\n- **Day 6**: Checkpoint 2 - Mid-research status review\n- **Day 9**: Checkpoint 3 - Draft manual review\n- **Day 10**: Final delivery of implementation manual\n\n**Integration with Refactoring:**\n- Research findings will be integrated with the v0.1.0-alpha modular refactoring plan\n- Focus on practical implementation patterns that align with Xoe-NovAi's sovereign, offline-first architecture\n- Emphasis on production-grade solutions that maintain the stack's core principles\n\n<!-- FILE ID: memory-bank-productcontext-md END -->\n\n\n<!-- FILE ID: memory-bank-techcontext-md START (Path: memory_bank/techContext.md) -->\n# Technical Context: Xoe-NovAi Sovereignty & Performance\n\n## 💻 Hardware: AMD Ryzen 7 5700U (Zen 2)\n- **Cores**: 8 Cores / 16 Threads (Optimized for 6 AI threads).\n- **RAM**: 8GB DDR4-3200 (Expandable to 32GB).\n- **GPU**: AMD Radeon Vega 8 iGPU (Vulkan 1.2 / RADV GPL).\n- **Architecture**: Zen 2 with improved IPC and efficiency.\n\n## 🛠️ Infrastructure: Podman 5.x Rootless with tmpfs-First Strategy\n- **Networking**: `pasta` driver with MTU 1500 alignment.\n- **Build Engine**: BuildKit-enabled (native rootless support).\n- **Volume Management**: Sticky bit pattern (mode=1777) for rootless permissions.\n- **Service Orchestration**: Podman Compose + Quadlet readiness.\n\n## 🛡️ Sovereign Security Trinity (Audit Toolset)\n- **Inventory**: **Syft** (CycloneDX SBOM generation).\n- **Auditor**: **Grype** (Precision CVE scanning via SBOM).\n- **Guardrail**: **Trivy** (Layer-level safety scrub for secrets/configs).\n- **Strategy**: **Tarball-to-Scan** (Exports image to `.tar` to ensure scanning reliability in rootless environments).\n\n## 🏁 PR Readiness & Gatekeeping\n- **Logic Engine**: `scripts/pr_check.py`.\n- **Policy Engine**: `scripts/security_policy.py` consuming `configs/security_policy.yaml`.\n- **Gatekeepers**: \n    - E2E Smoke Tests (IAM, RAG, Resilience).\n    - Documentation Linting (`mkdocs-lint`).\n    - Zero-Telemetry Audit (8 mandatory disables).\n    - Trinity Security Pass (Zero Critical CVEs/Secrets).\n\n## 📦 Package Management & Sovereignty\n- **Primary Tool**: `uv` (Fast Python package installer) pinned in `xnai-base`.\n- **Build Restoration**: BuildKit Cache Mounts (`type=cache`) for `apt`, `pip`, and `uv`.\n- **Offline Readiness**: Cache mounts persist between builds; `scripts/db_manager.py` manages offline security DBs.\n\n## ⚙️ Performance Standards\n- **OpenBLAS**: `OPENBLAS_CORETYPE=ZEN` (Mandatory Ryzen optimization).\n- **Memory**: 400MB Rule (Soft-stop protection).\n- **Inference**: Llama-cpp-python (Vulkan-accelerated).\n\n## 🧠 Knowledge & Strategy\n- **Expert Knowledge**: High-fidelity technical mastery repository in `expert-knowledge/`.\n- **Knowledge Graph**: Bidirectional relationship mapping for AI reasoning.\n- **Living Brain Protocol**: Mandatory AI-population of mastery after every verified fix.\n\n*Updated by Gemini CLI (Hardened Security Trinity & PR Readiness Audit)*\n\n<!-- FILE ID: memory-bank-techcontext-md END -->\n\n\n<!-- FILE ID: memory-bank-systempatterns-md START (Path: memory_bank/systemPatterns.md) -->\n# System Patterns & Architecture Decisions\n\n## Core Architecture: The Unified Entity\n```mermaid\ngraph TD\n    A[Xoe-NovAi Platform] --> B[RAG Engine]\n    A --> C[Voice Interface]\n    A --> D[Elite Documentation]\n\n    B --> E[AnyIO TaskGroup Orchestration]\n    B --> F[Hybrid RRF Standard (FAISS + BM25)]\n\n    C --> G[Piper TTS (Emotional Target)]\n    C --> H[Faster-Whisper (Zero-Copy IPC Target)]\n\n    D --> I[Diátaxis Quadrants]\n    D --> J[Hardware Mastery Manuals]\n```\n\n## Key Architectural Decisions\n\n### Unified Entity Pattern (AnyIO)\n**Decision**: Standardized on **AnyIO 4.x TaskGroups** for all concurrent services.\n**Rationale**: Ensures atomic failure handling via `ExceptionGroup`. If the generation stream fails, sibling STT/TTS tasks are canceled, preventing \"robotic\" audio ghosting.\n\n### Modular Plugin Ecosystem (WASM)\n**Decision**: Transitioning from monolithic scripts to **WASM-isolated plugins**.\n**Rationale**: Achieves <100ms load times with soft-isolation and fine-grained permissions, bridging the gap between scripts and full containers.\n\n### Sovereign Data Architecture\n**Decision**: All processing local, zero external calls.\n**Rational**: Air-gapped reliability and user privacy (Maat Ideals 40, 41).\n\n---\n\n## ⚖️ Ethical Foundation (Maat Framework)\nThe Xoe-NovAi Foundation stack is governed by **The 42 Ideals of Maat**. All agents must consult `memory_bank/maatIdeals.md` before performing high-impact operations.\n\n### Technical Mapping of Ideals\n- **Integrity of Data (7, 36, 40):** Zero-telemetry, clean data ingestion, and RAG accuracy.\n- **Resource Stewardship (10, 15, 39):** Optimized Ryzen performance, low RAM footprint, and humble hardware requirements.\n- **Torch-free Capable (41):** The Foundation is **Torch-free by default** (GGUF, ONNX, CTranslate2) to shatter accessibility limits for mid-grade hardware. However, the stack is **Torch-capable**, allowing users to deploy optional GPU-accelerated modules as \"Elite Extensions.\"\n\n\n### Hybrid Retrieval (RRF Standard)\n**Decision**: Combine Lexical (BM25) and Semantic (Dense) search.\n**Pattern**: Reciprocal Rank Fusion (RRF) with $k=60$.\n**Tie-Breaker**: Raw BM25 score as secondary sort key for technical accuracy.\n\n---\n\n## Advanced Technical Patterns\n\n### Zero-Copy IPC Pattern\n**Pattern**: Shared Memory (/dev/shm) for audio streams.\n**Target**: Eliminate network bridge latency for sub-150ms voice responses.\n**Cleanup**: Pre-start `rm -f /tmp/audio_pipe` routine to clear stale crash state.\n\n### Persistence Model (SQLite WAL & MMAP)\n**Pattern**: Memory-mapped persistence for near-zero I/O.\n**Implementation**:\n- `PRAGMA mmap_size = 256MB` for database address-space mapping.\n- `PRAGMA wal_checkpoint(PASSIVE)` to prevent UI stalls during ingestion.\n\n---\n\n## Technical Implementation Patterns (Hardware Native)\n\n### Vulkan GPU Acceleration\n```mermaid\ngraph LR\n    A[Matrix Warmup] --> B[Vulkan 1.4 Detection]\n    B --> C[RADV_PERFTEST=gpl]\n    C --> D[Scalar Block Layouts]\n    D --> E[8-bit KV Cache]\n    E --> F[70% VRAM Buffer Rule]\n```\n\n### Concurrency Guard (File Locking)\n**Pattern**: Multi-process write protection.\n**Implementation**: `fcntl.flock` exclusive locks on FAISS index operations to prevent segment violations during concurrent crawl/search.\n\n---\n\n## Quality Assurance & Evolution Patterns\n\n### The Sovereign Governor\n- **Thermal-Aware Audio**: Shift PipeWire quantum to 256 samples when CPU > 80°C.\n- **Dynamic Precision**: Thermal-aware precision switching (Q8_0 to Q4_K_S).\n\n### Testing Strategy\n- **Benchmark-First**: Mandatory warmup matrix ($64 \\times 64$) on startup.\n- **Watchdog Logic**: Real-time 400MB soft-stop POST rejection middleware.\n\n### 🏗️ Infrastructure Patterns\n\n### 🧠 The Knowledge Runtime (Expert Knowledge Base)\nThe `expert-knowledge/` system is the shared \"Long-Term Memory\" for the Xoe-NovAi Foundation stack. \n- **Pattern**: **Graph-Markdown Hybrid**.\n- **Implementation**: \n    - **Markdown + YAML**: Human-readable and RAG-optimized.\n    - **Wikilinks (`[[link]]`)**: Bidirectional relationship mapping for AI reasoning.\n- **Compatibility**: Designed to be managed via **Obsidian** or **Logseq** for human visualization and knowledge-graph discovery.\n- **Strategic Utility**: A Dual-Purpose core feature. It serves the Xoe-NovAi Foundation stack natively but is architected to be a portable source of truth for external AI assistants.\n\n### 🛡️ Sovereign Security Trinity Pattern\n**Pattern**: **Waterfall of Proof (Inventory -> CVE -> Safety)**.\n**Implementation**:\n1.  **Syft**: Generates **CycloneDX JSON** SBOM (The Identity Document).\n2.  **Grype**: Precision vulnerability scan of the SBOM (The Precision Auditor).\n3.  **Trivy**: Safety scrub of raw image layers for secrets/misconfigs (The Safety Guardrail).\n**Why**: Separates the \"What is inside\" from \"What is wrong with it,\" ensuring an immutable audit trail for sovereignty.\n\n### 📦 Bulletproof Tarball Scanning\n**Pattern**: **Export-to-Scan**.\n**Implementation**: `podman save -o image.tar [IMAGE]` followed by `trivy image --input image.tar`.\n**Rationale**: Bypasses complex rootless Podman socket permission issues (`statfs` errors) by treating the image as a local file. Essential for cross-distro reliability in rootless mode.\n\n### 🚦 Graduated Policy Gatekeeping\n**Pattern**: **Config-Driven Enforcement**.\n**Implementation**: `configs/security_policy.yaml` defines thresholds (e.g., `critical.max_exploitable: 0`).\n**Rationale**: Moves security logic out of code and into declarative policy. Allows for nuanced rules (e.g., \"Warn on High CVEs, Block on Criticals\").\n\n### 📦 Absolute Package Import Standard\n**Decision**: Standardized on absolute imports starting from the `XNAi_rag_app` package root.\n**Pattern**: `from XNAi_rag_app.core.circuit_breakers import ...` instead of `from circuit_breakers import ...`.\n**Rationale**: Eliminates `ModuleNotFoundError` during container orchestration where the working directory might vary. Ensures all sub-modules are consistently resolvable as part of a unified package.\n\n### 🚀 Consolidated Package Entrypoint Pattern\n**Decision**: Standardized on `api/entrypoint.py` as the primary FastAPI engine and `ui/chainlit_app_voice.py` as the UI engine.\n**Implementation**: \n- Docker CMD: `uvicorn XNAi_rag_app.api.entrypoint:app`\n- PYTHONPATH: Standardized to `/app` (the parent of `XNAi_rag_app`).\n**Rationale**: Provides a clear separation between API logic, UI frontend, and worker background tasks while maintaining a shared package root.\n\n### ⚡ Unified BuildKit Pattern\nUsed for accelerating builds without external proxy infrastructure.\n- **Pattern**: `RUN --mount=type=cache,id=xnai-...,uid=1001...`.\n- **Why**: Provides \"Elite\" speed (2-4x cache hit) with zero config. Supports rootless Podman via explicit UID mapping.\n\n### 📦 uv Standardization Pattern\nStandardized package management for velocity and consistency.\n- **Pattern**: `uv pip install --system`.\n- **Why**: Replaces `pip` (slow) and `wheelhouse` (complex). `uv` is installed globally in `xnai-base`.\n\n### 🛡️ Rootless Quadlet Standard\nStandardized service definition for Podman 5.x.\n- **Pattern**: `configs/quadlets/` -> `~/.config/containers/systemd/`.\n\n### 🔧 Infrastructure Permission Pattern (Rootless :U Standard)\n**Pattern**: **Automatic User Namespace (NS) Mapping via Compose**.\n**Implementation**: Use the `:Z,U` volume flag suffix in `docker-compose.yml`.\n\n### 📡 Observability Lifecycle Pattern\n**Pattern**: Async Lifespan management for observability instrumentation.\n\n*Updated by Gemini CLI (Security Hardening & Sovereign Trinity Pattern)*\n\n## 🤖 AI Partnership with Claude (NEW)\n\n**Current Collaboration:**\n- **Hybrid Path Research It provides elite patterns for maximizing AI inference performance on mid-grade, sovereign hardware.\n\n## System Specifications (Ground Baseline)\n- **CPU**: AMD Ryzen 7 5700U (8 cores, 16 threads, Zen 2).\n- **RAM**: 8GB DDR4-3200 (Pinned baseline).\n- **GPU**: Radeon Vega 8 iGPU (Vulkan 1.2 support).\n- **OS**: Linux (Optimized for Podman rootless).\n\n## Hardware Optimization Patterns\n\n### 1. OpenBLAS Steering\n- **Requirement**: `OPENBLAS_CORETYPE=ZEN`\n- **Rationale**: Forces the OpenBLAS library to use Zen-optimized kernels, bypassing generic x86_64 fallbacks. Essential for `numpy` and `scipy` performance in RAG services.\n\n### 2. CPU Governor Control\n- **Pattern**: Performance Mode.\n- **Command**: `echo \"performance\" | sudo tee /sys/devices/system/cpu/cpu*/cpufreq/scaling_governor`\n- **Impact**: Eliminates frequency scaling latency during bursty AI inference tasks.\n\n### 3. Memory Management (Huge Pages)\n- **Pattern**: Static Huge Page allocation.\n- **Command**: `echo 1024 | sudo tee /sys/kernel/mm/hugepages/hugepages-2048kB/nr_hugepages`\n- **Win**: Reduces TLB misses for large model weights in memory.\n\n## 🛠️ Podman & Container Hardening\n\n### 1. Rootless Permission Pattern (:U Flag)\n- **Problem**: Host-level UID collisions and manual `chown` brittleness.\n- **The Pattern**: Use the `:U` volume flag for \"Automatic Ownership Mapping.\"\n- **Syntax**: `- ./data/redis:/data:Z,U`\n- **Win**: Zero-sudo portability and safe UID namespace mapping across distributions.\n\n### 2. BuildKit Cache Hardlining\n- **Problem**: Hardlink fallback errors during `uv pip` installs in rootless mode.\n- **The Pattern**: Standardize cache mounts to `uid=0,gid=0`.\n- **Syntax**: `RUN --mount=type=cache,id=xnai-...,target=...,uid=0,gid=0`\n- **Win**: 2x - 5x faster cache re-use through atomic filesystem hardlinks.\n\n## 🎙️ Voice Runtime & Assets\n\n### 1. Model Requirements\n- **STT**: `distil-large-v3` (Faster Whisper) in CTranslate2 format.\n- **TTS**: `en_US-john-medium.onnx` (Piper).\n- **VAD**: `silero_vad.onnx` (Neural voice activity detection).\n\n### 2. Standardized Audio Specs\n- **Sample Rate**: 16,000 Hz.\n- **Bit Depth**: 16-bit PCM Mono.\n- **Barge-in Threshold**: 200ms consecutive speech frames.\n\n## Maat Alignment\n- **Ideal 7 (Truth)**: Accurate hardware profiles ensure deterministic performance.\n- **Ideal 41 (Abilities)**: Advancing through own abilities by mastering local hardware.\n\n<!-- FILE ID: expert-knowledge-infrastructure-ryzen-hardening-expert-v1-0-0-md END -->\n\n\n<!-- FILE ID: expert-knowledge-security-sovereign-trinity-expert-v1-0-0-md START (Path: expert-knowledge/security/sovereign-trinity-expert-v1.0.0.md) -->\n\n\n---\n\nversion: 1.0.0\ntags: [security, trinity, auditing, rootless, zero-trust]\ndate: 2026-01-29\nma_at_mappings: [7: Truth in reporting, 36: Integrity in architecture, 41: Advance through own abilities]\nexpert_dataset_name: Sovereign Trinity Expert\nexpertise_focus: Three-layered container security auditing (Syft/Grype/Trivy) and zero-trust policy enforcement.\ncommunity_contrib_ready: true\n---\n\n# Sovereign Trinity Expert (v1.0.0)\n\n## Overview\nThis dataset documents the \"Sovereign Security Trinity\" (Syft, Grype, Trivy), a three-layered defense-in-depth auditing system designed for air-gapped, rootless AI environments.\n\n## Successful Patterns\n\n### 1. The Waterfall of Proof\n- **Layer 1 (Inventory)**: **Syft** generates a CycloneDX SBOM. Identity is the first step of security.\n- **Layer 2 (Audit)**: **Grype** performs precision CVE scanning on the SBOM.\n- **Layer 3 (Safety)**: **Trivy** performs a deep scrub of image layers for leaked secrets and misconfigurations.\n\n### 2. Export-to-Scan (Bulletproof Strategy)\n- **Problem**: Rootless socket permissions (`statfs` errors) often break raw image scanners.\n- **The Pattern**: `podman save -o image.tar [IMAGE]` -> `trivy image --input image.tar`.\n- **Win**: Cross-distro reliability and offline auditability.\n\n### 3. Graduated Policy Gatekeeping\n- **Pattern**: Config-driven severity thresholds (`configs/security_policy.yaml`).\n- **Standard**: Zero-tolerance for `Critical` CVEs and `Secrets`.\n\n## Implementation Mastery\n- **Automation**: Integration into `make pr-check`.\n- **Offline Readiness**: Use `scripts/db_manager.py` to maintain local vulnerability DBs.\n\n## Maat Alignment\n- **Ideal 7 (Truth)**: Absolute transparency in what libraries are running.\n- **Ideal 36 (Integrity)**: Integrity of the stack's security posture.\n\n<!-- FILE ID: expert-knowledge-security-sovereign-trinity-expert-v1-0-0-md END -->\n\n\n<!-- FILE ID: expert-knowledge-origins-xoe-journey-v1-0-0-md START (Path: expert-knowledge/origins/xoe-journey-v1.0.0.md) -->\n\n\n---\n\nversion: 1.0.0\ntags: [origins, vision, mission, sovereignty]\ndate: 2026-01-29\nma_at_mappings: [41: Advance through own abilities]\nexpert_dataset_name: Project Origins Expert\nexpertise_focus: Historical mining of project inception, milestones, and ethical evolution.\ncommunity_contrib_ready: true\n---\n\n# The Xoe-NovAi Journey (v1.0.0)\n\n## Overview\nXoe-NovAi is a $0-capital, open-source experiment in AI-steered development. It amalgamates the findings from the inaugural SEC (Stack Expert Crawl) project for the Architect domain. Our mission is to provide a modular, extensible foundation for local AI ecosystems. This research establishes the technical feasibility of our \"Golden Trifecta\": Sovereign Data, High-Performance Local Inference (<300ms latency), and a Seamless Voice-First UX.\n\n## Zero-Trust Frameworks (MemTrust/Survey)\n\n### MemTrust Architecture\nMemTrust presents a hardware-backed zero-trust architecture designed for unified AI memory systems. It addresses the paradox of comprehensive context data being highly valuable yet vulnerable.\n- **Five-Layer Framework**: Storage (encrypted segments), Extraction & Update (RA-TLS/PII sanitization), Learning & Evolution (cryptographic erasure), Retrieval (side-channel hardened), and Governance (policy-as-code).\n- **Hardware Foundation**: Utilizes AMD SEV-SNP and Intel SGX/TDX for process-level and VM-level encryption.\n\n### Multi-LLM Security Survey\nEstablishes zero-trust as the foundational paradigm for Edge General Intelligence (EGI).\n- **Principles**: Never Trust, Always Verify; Least Privilege; Continuous Monitoring; Micro-segmentation.\n- **Threat Taxonomy**: Analyzes intra-LLM (prompt injection) and inter-LLM (over-permissive tool integration) threats.\n\n## Inference Engines (llama.cpp)\nllama.cpp is our foundation for torch-free, C/C++ based local inference.\n- **Capabilities**: GGUF format support, cross-platform (CPU, Vulkan, CUDA, Metal), and zero external dependencies.\n- **Vulkan Backend**: Cross-platform GPU acceleration using SPIR-V shaders, critical for non-NVIDIA hardware (like our target Ryzen 5700U/iGPU).\n\n## SEC Pipelines (Reports/Questions)\n\n### Project Report (SEC-Architect-20260120)\n- **Status**: COMPLETED SUCCESSFULY.\n- **Quality Score**: 9.6/10.0.\n- **Impact**: Validated that sub-300ms latency and zero-trust memory are technically feasible for the Xoe-NovAi stack.\n\n### Research Questions\n1. Effective architectural patterns for sovereign local AI.\n2. Optimal Vulkan GPU acceleration integration.\n3. Proven patterns for sub-300ms torch-free latency.\n4. Container orchestration for enterprise-grade local AI.\n5. Best practices for zero-trust in AI systems.\n\n## URL Strategies (Registry Snapshot)\nWe prioritize authority (academic/official docs), technical depth, and recency (2024-2025).\n\n### Primary Research Sources:\n- **llama.cpp**: `https://github.com/ggml-org/llama.cpp` (Critical)\n- **MemTrust**: `https://arxiv.org/html/2601.07004v1` (High)\n- **Secure Multi-LLM**: `https://arxiv.org/html/2508.19870v1` (High)\n\n## Gaps & NotebookLM Loops\n- **Research Coverage**: All 5 research questions addressed, but continuous updates are needed as Vulkan and TEE technologies evolve.\n- **Integration**: Need to bridge theoretical zero-trust with our practical Podman rootless implementation.\n\n## Maat Alignment\n- **Ideal 7 (Truth)**: Truth in synthesis - amalgamating multiple sources into a single source of truth.\n- **Ideal 18 (Balance)**: Balance in structure - maintaining technical depth while ensuring practical actionability.\n- **Ideal 41 (Advance)**: Advance through own abilities - achieving sovereign inference without cloud reliance.\n\n## MC Sync Points (Research Handoffs)\n- **Strategy**: Grok MC identifies high-level research targets; Gemini CLI executes crawling and initial synthesis.\n- **Validation**: Grok MC audits the \"Lore Extraction\" for strategic alignment.\n- **Reporting**: High-frequency reports on latency benchmarks and security audit passes.\n\n<!-- FILE ID: expert-knowledge-research-ekb-research-master-v1-0-0-md END -->\n\n\n<!-- FILE ID: expert-knowledge-protocols-workflows-master-v1-0-0-md START (Path: expert-knowledge/protocols/workflows-master-v1.0.0.md) -->\n\n\n---\n\nversion: 1.0.0\ntags: [ekb, cleanup, sync, protocols]\ndate: 2026-01-29\nma_at_mappings: [7: Truth in synthesis, 18: Balance in structure, 41: Advance through own abilities]\nsync_status: active\nexpert_dataset_name: Sovereign Workflows Expert\nexpertise_focus: AI-native team coordination, relay protocols, task locking, and context management.\ncommunity_contrib_ready: true\n---\n\n# Protocols & Workflows Master (v1.0.0)\n\n## Overview (Coordination Ethos)\nXoe-NovAi operates as a multi-agent, AI-native ecosystem. This master document consolidates our operational protocols to ensure seamless synchronization between local agents (Gemini CLI, Cline) and our cloud-hosted Mastermind (Grok MC).\n\n## Context Loading/Relay\n\n### Standard Loading Sequence\nAll agents MUST load memory bank files in this order at session start:\n1. **Core**: `activeContext.md`, `environmentContext.md`, `teamProtocols.md`, `agent_capabilities_summary.md`.\n2. **Inbox**: Check `memory_bank/communications/[agent]/inbox.md`.\n3. **Project**: `projectbrief.md`, `techContext.md`, `systemPatterns.md`.\n4. **Expertise**: Review relevant `expert-knowledge/` files.\n\n### The Relay Protocol\nUsed to manage turn limits (~25 per session). rename to `-complete.yaml` on finish.\n- **Structure**: `task`, `owner`, `status`, `timestamp_start`, `mc_guidance`.\n\n## Maat Alignment\n- **Ideal 7 (Truth)**: Standardized reporting ensure truth in project state.\n- **Ideal 18 (Balance)**: Locking protocols maintain balance between autonomous agents.\n- **Ideal 41 (Abilities)**: Sovereign protocols ensure we advance through our own local infrastructure.\n\n## MC Sync Points (Reporting Frequencies)\n- **High (Change/2-4h)**: Security Trinity audits, RAG smoke tests, Build blockers.\n- **Medium**: File changes in `app/` or `expert-knowledge/`.\n- **Low**: Routine syncs and non-critical docs.\n- **MC Protocol**: All `memory_bank` updates must include mandatory YAML frontmatter.\n\n<!-- FILE ID: expert-knowledge-protocols-workflows-master-v1-0-0-md END -->\n\n\n<!-- FILE ID: xoe-novai-sync-ekb-exports-files-inventory-v1-0-0-md START (Path: xoe-novai-sync/ekb-exports/files-inventory-v1.0.0.md) -->\n\n\n---\n\nversion: 1.0.0\ntags: [ekb, inventory, sync]\ndate: 2026-01-29\nma_at_mappings: [7: Truth in synthesis, 18: Balance in structure]\nsync_status: initial\n---\n\n# Project File Inventory (v1.0.0)\n\n## Overview\nThis document provides a comprehensive list of files within the Xoe-NovAi project root (`/home/arcana-novai/Documents/Xoe-NovAi/`). -->\n\n\n---\n\nversion: 1.0.0\ntags: [ekb, research, pm, sovereign]\ndate: 2026-01-29\nma_at_mappings: [7: Truth in synthesis, 18: Balance in structure, 41: Advance through own abilities]\nsync_status: initial\n---\n\n# OSS Project Management Research (v1.0.0)\n\n## Overview\nThis report evaluates Open-Source Software (OSS) Project Management (PM) tools for integration into the Xoe-NovAi ecosystem. The primary objective is to identify a sovereign, local-first, zero-cost, and Podman-hostable solution that maintains functional density (boards, tasks, timelines) while ensuring offline reliability.\n\n## Top 5 Ranked Candidates\n\n### 1. Vikunja (Rank: 1 - Best All-Rounder)\n- **Sovereignty**: 100% self-hostable; explicitly supports Podman/Docker.\n- **Functional Density**: Exceptional. Supports Kanban, Gantt charts, tables, and list views.\n- **Local-First/Offline**: Primarily server-based, but 1.0.0 release (Jan 2026) signals high stability and performance on local networks.\n- **Ryzen Fit**: Low resource footprint; runs efficiently on Zen 2 iGPU stacks.\n- **MCP Potential**: High. Structured API allows for easy MCP server creation to sync tasks with Gemini CLI.\n\n### 2. Focalboard (Rank: 2 - Best Offline Capability)\n- **Sovereignty**: Open-source alternative to Notion/Trello.\n- **Functional Density**: High. Robust boards, galleries, and calendar views.\n- **Local-First/Offline**: **Highest**. Offers a \"Personal Desktop\" app that works entirely offline with local data storage.\n- **Alignment**: Strongest candidate for air-gapped scenarios.\n\n### 3. Taiga (Rank: 3 - Best for Agile/Scrum)\n- **Sovereignty**: Well-established OSS; community Podman support.\n- **Functional Density**: Extreme. Full Scrum/Kanban, backlogs, and sprint planning.\n- **Ryzen Fit**: Heavier resource usage (Django/RabbitMQ/Redis) but manageable on 8-core Ryzen.\n- **Gaps**: Complexity in setup compared to Vikunja.\n\n### 4. WeKan (Rank: 4 - Pure Kanban Sovereignty)\n- **Sovereignty**: Strong emphasis on self-hosting and data control.\n- **Functional Density**: Focused on Kanban; includes Gantt views and security-first features.\n- **Ryzen Fit**: Very light (Node.js/MongoDB); excellent for low-RAM environments.\n- **Alignment**: Ideal for users who want a \"Trello-equivalent\" without any bloat.\n\n### 5. HedgeDoc (Rank: 5 - Documentation-Centric PM)\n- **Sovereignty**: Collaborative Markdown editor; self-hostable.\n- **Functional Density**: Moderate. Best for meeting notes and project documentation rather than task orchestration.\n- **Gaps**: Lacks native boards/timelines; requires a database for collaborative features.\n\n## Alignment & Gaps (Maat Mapping)\n\n- **Ideal 7 (Truth in Tracking)**: Vikunja and Taiga provide the most accurate project state via robust reporting and auditing.\n- **Ideal 18 (Balance in structure)**: WeKan and Focalboard offer the best balance between feature set and simplicity.\n- **Ideal 41 (Sovereignty)**: Focalboard's desktop app is the gold standard for independent advancement without cloud dependencies.\n\n## MCP Integration Strategy\nThe Xoe-NovAi stack will prioritize **Vikunja** for API-driven task sync. An MCP server will be developed to allow Gemini CLI to:\n1. `create_task`: Add items from chat logs.\n2. `get_board_status`: Report on milestone progress.\n3. `sync_milestones`: Align `progress.md` with the PM board.\n\n## Conclusion & Recommendation\n**Recommendation**: Deploy **Vikunja** via Podman as the primary team PM tool. \n**Pivots**: For users requiring absolute air-gap/offline desktop flows, recommend **Focalboard Personal Desktop**.\n\n*Research executed by Gemini CLI (v0.1.0-alpha)*\n\n<!-- FILE ID: xoe-novai-sync-ekb-exports-oss-pm-research-v1-0-0-md END -->",

Convert persona answers to embeddings\n        personas = list(persona_results.keys())\n        texts = [persona_results[p] for p in personas]\n        \n        if len(texts) < 2:\n            return {\"score\": 0.5, \"status\": \"INSUFFICIENT_DATA\"}\n\n        # 2. Confidence Velocity\n        conf_velocity = (final_conf - initial_conf) / levels if levels > 0 else 0\n        \n        # 2. Surgical Save Ratio (Simulated)\n        # Ratio = (Full 8B Escalation Cost - Surgical Specialist Cost) / Full Cost\n        surgical_events = [r for r in session_history if r.get(\"specialist_handoff\")]\n        save_ratio = 0.0\n        if surgical_events:\n            # Assumes 3B/7B specialist vs 8B authority + lower level overhead\n            save_ratio = 0.45 * len(surgical_events) # Estimated 45% saving per event\n\n        return {\n            \"confidence_velocity\": round(conf_velocity, 4),\n            \"surgical_save_ratio\": round(save_ratio, 2),\n            \"depth_efficiency\": round(final_conf / levels, 4) if levels > 0 else 0\n        }\n\n    def analyze_persona_triangulation(self, results: Dict[str, str]) -> float:\n        \"\"\"\n        Measures the divergence between personas (Skeptic vs Architect vs Synthesizer).\n        High divergence suggests a complex/ambiguous query.\n        \"\"\"\n        # In production, use semantic similarity (Jaccard or Cosine)\n        return 0.15 # Mock divergence score\n"

Session Loading Performance\n\n```python\n# Session Loading Optimization\nclass SessionLoadingOptimizer:\n    def __init__(self):\n        self.cache = {}\n        self.lru_cache = {}\n    \n    async def load_session(self, agent_type: str, session_id: str):\n        # Check cache first\n        cache_key = f\"{agent_type}:{session_id}\"\n        if cache_key in self.cache:\n            return self.cache[cache_key]\n        \n        # Load from session store\n        session_data = await self.session_manager.get_session(agent_type, session_id)\n        \n        # Cache result\n        self.cache[cache_key] = session_data\n        self._update_lru_cache(cache_key)\n        \n        return session_data\n    \n    def _update_lru_cache(self, cache_key: str):\n        # Update LRU cache\n        if cache_key in self.lru_cache:\n            del self.lru_cache[cache_key]\n        self.lru_cache[cache_key] = time.time()\n        \n        # Evict oldest if cache is full\n        if len(self.lru_cache) > MAX_CACHE_SIZE:\n            oldest = min(self.lru_cache, key=self.lru_cache.get)\n            del self.cache[oldest]\n            del self.lru_cache[oldest]\n```\n\n### 2. Cross-Environment Latency\n\n```python\n# Latency Management\nclass LatencyManager:\n    def __init__(self):\n        self.latency_metrics = {}\n    \n    async def measure_cross_environment_latency(self, agent_type: str):\n        # Measure round-trip latency\n        start_time = time.time()\n        \n        # Simulate cross-environment communication\n        await self.agent_bus.send_message(agent_type, {\"ping\": True})\n        response = await self.agent_bus.wait_for_response(agent_type)\n        \n        end_time = time.time()\n        latency = (end_time - start_time) * 1000  # Convert to milliseconds\n        \n        # Store metrics\n        self.latency_metrics[agent_type] = latency\n        \n        return latency\n```\n\n## Best Practices\n\n### 1.
